      <li class="menu-item menu-item-type-taxonomy menu-item-object-category current-post-ancestor current-menu-parent current-post-parent menu-item-has-children menu-item-17608" id="menu-item-17608">

      <div class="hfeed" id="content">
       <div class="post-2832 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-diy-projects category-home-decor tag-diy tag-frugal tag-glass tag-gorilla-glue tag-hurricane tag-tutorial tag-vases entry">
        <h1 class="entry-title">
         Hurricane Vases! {Frugal DIY Tutorial}
        </h1>
        <div class="post-info">
         <span class="date published time" title="2010-09-08T20:06:31+00:00">
          September 8, 2010
         </span>
         By
         <a class="url fn author" href="http://myblessedlife.net/meet-myra" rel="author">
          Myra Hope
         </a>
         <span class="post-comments">
          <a href="http://myblessedlife.net/2010/09/hurricane-vases-frugal-diy-tutorial.html#comments">
           155 Comments
          </a>
         </span>
        </div>
        <div class="entry-content">
         <p class="first-child ">
          <span class="cap" title="F">
           <span>
            F
           </span>
          </span>
          or years, Ive coveted the gorgeous hurricane vases available at Williams-Sonoma. I mean, whats there not to love? Well, to be perfectly honestthe price.
          <strong>
           Williams-Sonoma hurricanes range from $70.00 to $118.00! Ouch-y. Too pricey for my thrift-store-loving wallet.
          </strong>
          So when I saw
          <a href="http://www.decorchick.com/decorating/dollar-store-hurricanes/" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">
           the hurricane brilliance over at Decor Chick
          </a>
          , I knew I had try this project for myself.
         </p>
         <p style="text-align: center;">
          <a href="http://myblessedlife.net/wp-content/uploads/2012/10/hurricane-vases.jpg">
           <img alt="" class="aligncenter wp-image-13990" height="315" src="http://myblessedlife.net/wp-content/uploads/2012/10/hurricane-vases-550x366.jpg" title="hurricane vases" width="486"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p style="text-align: center;">
          Arent they pretty?
         </p>
         <p style="text-align: left;">
          Now Im going to show you how
          <strong>
           you can get your beautiful, hurricane vase party on at your house!!!
          </strong>
          Fun!
         </p>
         <p style="text-align: center;">
          <a href="http://s674.photobucket.com/albums/vv107/mmy308/?action=view&amp;current=afalldoor3.jpg" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">
           <img alt="Photobucket" border="0" class="aligncenter" height="395" src="http://i674.photobucket.com/albums/vv107/mmy308/afalldoor3.jpg" style="border: 0pt none;" width="511"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p style="text-align: left;">
          <strong>
           Supplies
          </strong>
          you need:
         </p>
         <ul>
          <li>
           <strong>
            Gorilla Glue
           </strong>
            Id never used Gorilla Glue before, so I was stepping out of my comfort zone. I bought GG (that dries white) at Hobby Lobby for $5.
           <strong>
            It is super easy to use and Im very happy with how it worked!
           </strong>
          </li>
          <li>
           <strong>
            Candle Sticks
           </strong>
            Over the last few months, Ive developed quite a collection of clear candle sticks  from thrift stores and the Dollar Tree.
          </li>
          <li>
           <strong>
            Glass vases
           </strong>
            I already had three vases from flowers that my sweet hubby has gotten me and I also picked up a few more from the Dollar Tree and Walmart.
          </li>
         </ul>
         <p style="text-align: left;">
          <strong>
           I followed the directions on the Gorilla Glue box
          </strong>
          which said to sparingly apply GG on one surface (the bottom of a vase)and then dampen the other surface (the candle stick) before putting them together. Then I centered the candlestick on the vase
         </p>
         <p style="text-align: left;">
          <a href="http://s674.photobucket.com/albums/vv107/mmy308/?action=view&amp;current=afalldoor2.jpg" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">
           <img alt="Photobucket" border="0" class="aligncenter" height="448" src="http://i674.photobucket.com/albums/vv107/mmy308/afalldoor2.jpg" style="border: 0pt none;" width="448"/>
          </a>
          You can see how
          <strong>
           the Gorilla Glue bubbles up and turns white.
          </strong>
          Thats why you dont need to use too much. Ask me how I know.
          <em>
           {blush}
          </em>
          Im the one who had to use a knife to cut off the excess white foamy glue. Ahem.
         </p>
         <p style="text-align: center;">
          <a href="http://s674.photobucket.com/albums/vv107/mmy308/?action=view&amp;current=IMG_6389.jpg" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">
           <img alt="Photobucket" border="0" class="aligncenter" height="447" src="http://i674.photobucket.com/albums/vv107/mmy308/IMG_6389.jpg" style="border: 0pt none;" width="298"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p style="text-align: left;">
          Then,
          <strong>
           carefully balance a large book on the candle stick to hold it together while the Gorilla Glue dries
          </strong>
          . The vase looks cloudy because I washed it and didnt let it completely dry before starting my project. Waiting patiently is not my forte
         </p>
         <p style="text-align: left;">
          For example, I lined up five vases to glue at the same time. I glued them. Put books on them. And left to run an errand.
          <strong>
           When I came home, a vase was broken and not one candle stick was still on top of a vase.
          </strong>
          The domino effect had happened. Oh and to make it even betterthree candlesticks were glued to the carpet.
          <em>
           {brilliant, I tell ya!}
          </em>
         </p>
         <p style="text-align: center;">
          <a href="http://myblessedlife.net/wp-content/uploads/2012/10/hurricane-vase-3.jpg">
           <img alt="" class="aligncenter wp-image-13988" height="315" src="http://myblessedlife.net/wp-content/uploads/2012/10/hurricane-vase-3-550x366.jpg" title="hurricane vase 3" width="486"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p style="text-align: center;">
          Love. Love. Love.
         </p>
         <p style="text-align: center;">
          Simple, natural, candle-lit beauty.
         </p>
         <p style="text-align: center;">
          <a href="http://myblessedlife.net/wp-content/uploads/2010/09/hurricane-vases.jpg">
           <img alt="" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-12853" height="599" src="http://myblessedlife.net/wp-content/uploads/2010/09/hurricane-vases.jpg" title="dollar store hurricane vases" width="400"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          <a class="pin-it-button" href="http://pinterest.com/pin/create/button/?url=http%3A%2F%2Fmyblessedlife.net%2F2010%2F09%2Fhurricane-vases-frugal-diy-tutorial.html&amp;media=http%3A%2F%2Fmyblessedlife.net%2Fwp-content%2Fuploads%2F2010%2F09%2Fhurricane-vases.jpg&amp;description=Dollar%20Store%20Hurricane%20Vases" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">
           <img alt="" border="0" src="//assets.pinterest.com/images/PinExt.png" title="Pin It"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p style="text-align: left;">
          These vases grace
          <a href="http://myblessedlife.net/2010/09/simplifying-my-bookcases.html" target="_blank">
           my simplified bookshelves
          </a>
          and are the perfect addition to
          <a href="http://myblessedlife.net/2010/09/simple-and-beautiful-fall-decor.html" target="_blank">
           my simple, frugal Fall decor
          </a>
          . I filled the vases with
          <strong>
           cinnamon sticks, berries, ribbon, pumpkins, gourds and corn
          </strong>
          . The only things I purchased this year for these two hurricanes, are the cinnamon sticks ($1.47) and the berries ($1.50). Cant beat that!
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Eight glass hurricane vases cost me less than $20!!!
          </strong>
          <em>
           {happy dance}
          </em>
          Plus the time I spent getting dried Gorilla Glue out of the carpet. Snort.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Have you ever used Gorilla Glue before?
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          Linked to:
         </p>
         <ul>

            Im Lovin It!
           </a>

            Money Saving Mom
           </a>
          </li>

           <p>
            I made three hurricane vases today! I love the way they look on my bookshelf and bathroom. Even my husband noticed and complimented them. He said he loved them even more when I told him what Id spent!
           </p>
           <p>
            I swiped some gorilla glue from my brother-in-law and returned it to him today.  I dont advocate stealing, but this was just borrowing. =) He actually told me I could keep it if I wanted itlol!
           </p>
          </div>
